## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / batch reactor ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is an ordinary differential equation describing how concentration A changes with time t, which is the core modeling object in chemical kinetics for batch/closed systems. With only (t, A) available, the most likely structures are empirical or mechanistic rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, saturation, inhibition) and/or explicit time dependence (time-varying rate coefficient, forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or excess reactant)
- Zero-order production: dA_dt = c0 (constant feed/formation over time)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition analog)
- First-order with source: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (formation plus linear loss, well-mixed with constant input)
- Second-order decay (single-species): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or dimerization surrogate)
- General n-th order power law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order not necessarily integer)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type) growth/decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating formation with depletion/limitation)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Saturating consumption (Monod-like in A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate limited by saturation/active sites; low-A linear, high-A capped)
- Substrate inhibition (Haldane-like in A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (rate decreases at high A due to self-inhibition/complexation)
- Time-varying first-order (nonstationary k): dA_dt = -(c0 * exp(c1 * t)) * A (rate coefficient changes over time due to ramping conditions/catalyst activation)
- Periodic forcing of rate: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally modulated kinetics, e.g., light/dosing cycles)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (linear in A), it indicates first-order kinetics; plotting dA_dt/A vs t reveals time-varying rate constants.
- If dA_dt is approximately constant over a range of A, it suggests zero-order behavior (rate limited by something other than A).
- Curvature where |dA_dt| grows faster than linearly with A suggests higher-than-first order (e.g., A**2 or A**n with n>1).
- A sign change of dA_dt at A = c indicates relaxation toward a steady state/equilibrium concentration (stable fixed point).
- Saturation appears when dA_dt becomes insensitive to A at high A; rational forms like A/(A+c) capture capped rates.
- Inhibition/self-poisoning is suggested when |dA_dt| increases with A at low A but decreases at high A; denominators containing A**2 are common.
- Autocatalysis is suggested when dA_dt is small near A≈0 but grows with A (factor A), often producing sigmoidal A(t).
- Explicit oscillations or nonmonotonicity in dA_dt at fixed A points to time-dependent forcing; include sin(c*t) or exp(c*t) modulation of rate coefficients.

**GT: `-0.2597*sqrt(A) + 0.9123*cos(log(A + 1))`**

This expression contains two key basis functions:
1. `sqrt(A)` — a square root term
2. `cos(log(A + 1))` — a cosine of logarithm term

Let me analyze the candidates. The GT has very specific transcendental functions (sqrt, cos, log). Most candidates are composed of polynomial terms in A (like A², A, 1/A⁵), terms involving t, and possibly exponentials or logarithms.

**Key observation:** The GT has NO dependence on `t` at all. So any candidate with `t`-dependent terms must have those terms set to zero (which is possible if the coefficients can be zeroed out). However, the GT contains `sqrt(A)` and `cos(log(A+1))`, which are transcendental functions that CANNOT be represented by polynomials, rational functions, or simple exponentials of A.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `sqrt(A)` and `cos(log(A+1))`:

- **Candidates 1-19, 21-31, 33, 37-38, 40-50**: These contain only polynomial terms in A (A², A, 1/A⁵), rational functions of t, and possibly Abs(A) (which equals A for A≥0). None contain sqrt(A) or cos(log(A+1)). These **cannot match**.

- **Candidate 20**: `A²*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2 + c3 + c4*exp(c5*Abs(c6*log(c7*Abs(A)+1))) + c8/A⁵`
  The exponential term is `exp(c5*|c6*log(c7*|A|+1)|)`. For A≥0, this becomes `exp(c5*|c6*log(c7*A+1)|)`. This is an exponential of a log, not cos(log). Cannot produce cos(log(A+1)) or sqrt(A). **No match.**

- **Candidate 32**: `A²*c0 + A*c1 + A + c2 + c3*log(A*c4+1) + c5*t/(c6*t+c7) + c8/(c6*t+c7) + c9/A⁵`
  Contains `log(A*c4+1)` but not `cos(log(...))` or `sqrt(A)`. **No match.**

- **Candidate 34**: Similar to 32 with `log(A*c4+1)`. **No match.**

- **Candidate 35**: `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4*|A|² + c5*|A|`. For A≥0: polynomial in A plus exponential in t. **No match.**

- **Candidate 36**: Polynomial in A plus exp(c4*t) and rational in t. **No match.**

- **Candidate 39**: `A²*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2 + c3*exp(A*c4) + c5`. Contains exp(A*c4), not the required functions. **No match.**

- **Candidate 41**: Polynomial in A plus exp in t. **No match.**

- **Candidate 43**: Polynomial in A with exp(c2*t) coefficients. **No match.**

- **Candidate 46**: Rational function of A. **No match.**

- **Candidate 49**: Contains `t*(A+c5)^c6` — power of A times t. Setting t-coefficient to 0 leaves polynomial. **No match.**

- **Candidate 7**: `A*c0 + A*c1*|A| + A^c2*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5 + c6*t/(c7*t+c8) + c9/(c7*t+c8)`. The term `A^c2*exp(c4*t)` — setting c4=0 gives `c3*A^c2`, which could be sqrt(A) with c2=0.5. But we still need cos(log(A+1)), which is absent. **No match.**
